  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d7cc4e84-fd1a-41b5-8087-8d502291744a'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText2827882923122625323" style="display:none"><b>Always be polite to dragons!</b><br /><br />That's what Daystar's mother taught him...and it's a very wise lesson--one that might just help him after his mom hands him a magic sword and kicks him out of the house. Especially because his house sits on the edge of the Enchanted Forest and his mother is Queen Cimorene.<br /><br />But the tricky part is figuring out what he's supposed to <i>do</i> with the magic sword. Where is he supposed to go? And why does everyone he meets seem to know who he is? <br /><br />It's going to take a particularly hotheaded fire-witch, a very verbose lizard, and a badly behaved baby dragon to help him figure it all out. <br /><br />And those good manners certainly won't hurt!</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/426254-can-anyone-tell-me-what-the-last-line-of">Can anyone tell me what the last line of this book is? I got this one many years ago at a library sale and it took me awhile to find the others to complete the series before reading them. It looks as if there might be some pages missing from the back of my copy.
The last line in my copy is, &quot;Smiling, I picked up the other two bundles and started after Shiara.&quot;</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_426254'><a id="like_count_community_question_426254" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/426254?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F169871.Talking_to_Dragons">like</a></span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/11421535-megan">Megan</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The last line changes depending on whether you have the original standalone book, published in 1985, which ends with "started after Shiara," or the on<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The last line changes depending on whether you have the original standalone book, published in 1985, which ends with "started after Shiara," or the one that was tweaked to become Enchanted Forest #4, which ends with "followed happily after."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<a href="/questions/1619157-silly-question-i-see-this-book-is-the">Silly question; I see this book is the last in the series, but was published several years before Dealing With Dragons. Is it a prequel that&#39;s meant to be read last?</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/605085-barry-haworth"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1539162721i/605085._UX100_CR0,16,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/605085-barry-haworth">Barry Haworth</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Agree with the other answer. This book was written first, but the author decided that the world was worth revisiting and wrote the rest of the series,<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Agree with the other answer. This book was written first, but the author decided that the world was worth revisiting and wrote the rest of the series, which give the back story of many of the characters. As it happens I read this one first but I do not think I enjoyed the series any less for reading the first written but last set book first.<br />That said, I do prefer the other books in the series, especially the first two in story time, <i>Dealing with Dragons</i> and <i>Searching for Dragons</i>. When reading the series I generally read just those two.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720670727" />
    <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword"><img alt="Iryna *Book and Sword*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547595130p2/57236678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720670727?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iryna *Book and Sword*" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword">Iryna *Book and Sword*</a>

<div id="review_1334792762" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1334792762" />
    <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy"><img alt="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475772748p2/4702933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1334792762?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy">MrsJoseph *grouchy*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2015-reading-challenges">2015-reading-challenges</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy?shelf=need-to-review">need-to-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1334792762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4988153588914124867"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookslifewine.com/r-talking-to-dragons/'>http://bookslifewine.com/r-talking-to...</a><br/><br/>3.5 stars rounded down to 3 stars<br/><br/>Tamika, <br/><br/>I've put the entire review for this final book in the series below. Hope you enjoy (cause you know I only posted this for you, lol)!<br/><br/><br/>NOTE: This review contains spoilers for the previous three (3) books in this series. Please read those books prior to reading this review.<br/><br/><br/><em>Talking to Dragons</em> is the fourth and final installation in the <em>Enchanted Forest Chronicles</em>. It's been a fun ride and I'm a little sad to see it end.<br/><br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText4988153588914124867" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookslifewine.com/r-talking-to-dragons/">http://bookslifewine.com/r-talking-to...</a><br /><br />3.5 stars rounded down to 3 stars<br /><br />Tamika, <br /><br />I've put the entire review for this final book in the series below. Hope you enjoy (cause you know I only posted this for you, lol)!<br /><br /><br />NOTE: This review contains spoilers for the previous three (3) books in this series. Please read those books prior to reading this review.<br /><br /><br /><em>Talking to Dragons</em> is the fourth and final installation in the <em>Enchanted Forest Chronicles</em>. It's been a fun ride and I'm a little sad to see it end.<br /><br />I found <em>Talking to Dragons</em> to be a lot more fun than <em>
  <a href="http://wp.me/p3GfI9-1Bj" rel="nofollow noopener">Calling on Dragons</a>
</em> but it never lived up to the expectation set by the first two books in the <a href="http://bookslifewine.com/reviews/series/the-enchanted-forest-chronicles/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Enchanted Forest Chronicles</em>
</a>.<br /><br /><em>Talking to Dragons</em> stars Daystar as the MC and starts 16-17 years after then ending of <em>Calling on Dragons</em>. Daystar is the son of previous MCs Queen Cimorene and King Mendenbar but he does not know this. All he knows is that he was the son of a wonderful mother named Cimorene. One day a wizard showed up at Daystar's cottage - and in surprise he watches his mother melt the wizard! Afterwards, Cimorene comes to Daystar with a magical sword and sends him off into the Enchanted Forest with no instruction.<br /><br />I really enjoyed <em>Talking to Dragons</em> but I found it...not as interesting. Wrede completely changed the tone of the series by making Daystar a boy, removing the gender role reversal theme* that the rest of the books in the series have. I was disappointed in that but I am glad that there is a male character in the series that young boys can relate to besides Mendenbar. There <em>is</em> a strong MC female character in the book - a fire witch named Shiara - but...she's a major PIA and nothing like the strong and capable Cimorene. Shiara is unbelievably rude (to everyone) and prone to either major attitude or tears at all times. When the reader meets Shiara, she can't do magic. Later she is able to perform magic but she has to be polite first. Instead of being happy that she can now perform magic (she was being chased by the magicians because she was unable to perform magic and thus unable to defend herself), Shiara gets a major attitude and starts bitching. <br /><br />Daystar, on the other hand, is closer to the male equivalent of Cimorene (with a little less sense, lol) - but he's lacking...imagination? Personality? Curiosity? Maybe all three. Daystar is not really curious as to who he is. He's not too concerned that his mother randomly sent him into the forest with a magic sword. Daystar isn't particularly interested in most things - it mostly feels like the adventures in <em>Talking to Dragons</em> happened <em>to</em> Daystar instead with Daystar. Daystar basically takes everything that happens to him in stride with no real surprise. <br /><br /><em>Talking to Dragons</em> was fun but it was also missing quite a bit of the whimsy of the previous novels, too. I would consider <em>Talking to Dragons</em> the most conventional and "canon-like" book in the series. Daystar is not an orphan or a farmboy but he's pretty close to the orphan farmboy trope. Daystar is given a magic sword and sent on an unknown quest. Almost everyone around him knows who/what he is before he does. The outcome of the "world" (the Enchanted Forest) is dependent on Daystar learning and doing specific things. As I said, very "canon-like."<br /><br />All in all, I enjoyed <em>Talking to Dragons</em> (a lot more than <em>Calling on Dragons</em>!!) and I'm sad to see the series end. Regardless of any complaints I had about this book, I did enjoy my read. I also purchased the series omnibus - rereads will occur!<br /><br /><br /><br />*Wrede wrote <em>Talking to Dragons</em> first, in 1985. The rest of the series - with gender themes - was written afterwards (1990, 1991 &amp; 1993) and then <em>Talking to Dragons</em> was re-written and re-released. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4988153588914124867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1703107359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1703107359" />
    <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz"><img alt="Ahmed  Ejaz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598778737p2/53694260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1703107359?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmed  Ejaz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmed  Ejaz" href="/user/show/53694260-ahmed-ejaz">Ahmed  Ejaz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53694260-ahmed-ejaz?shelf=full-lengths">full-lengths</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1703107359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6472915746496893408">WOW WOW WOW... ! <br/>My feelings are just out of control after reading the last book of this series. Maybe that's because this is my first series I have ever completed OR maybe I am over happy after reading a series of 4 books because this is my biggest series I had ever started. I don't know the exact reason. Never mind, who cares! I just wanted a good series and I think I have read one. <br/>Before saying anything else I must say this series is totally for children. Maybe some teens or adults will not </span>
  <span id="freeText6472915746496893408" style="display:none">WOW WOW WOW... ! <br />My feelings are just out of control after reading the last book of this series. Maybe that's because this is my first series I have ever completed OR maybe I am over happy after reading a series of 4 books because this is my biggest series I had ever started. I don't know the exact reason. Never mind, who cares! I just wanted a good series and I think I have read one. <br />Before saying anything else I must say this series is totally for children. Maybe some teens or adults will not enjoy this because some elements I felt were totally for children. But I also must say I enjoyed this no matter what.<br /><br />The last book was totally unexpected for me. At first, I couldn't understand that I am reading a right book or not because this book started just like a proper story not like a sequel to the 3rd book. I think persons who haven't read its previous books will also enjoy this book. But if you have read its previous books, you will understand it better and things may get predictable for you. <br /><br /><br /><u>▌<b>BOOK'S INFO.</b>▐</u><br /><br /><b>Chapters </b><br />--- 22 <br /><br /><b>Narration </b><br />--- First Person <br />I really liked it. Actually, it's my favourite.<br /><br /><b>Setting </b><br />--- Enchanted Forest <br />One of the amazing settings I have ever read.<br />This forest is full of magic. Magic floats in its atmosphere. Every place in this forest changes its position after some time. To get the more info. on this forest you should start from the 2nd book. 1st doesn't contain much info. about it.<br /><br /><br /><u>▌<b>MAJOR CHARACTERS</b>▐</u><br /><br /><b>Daystar</b><br />Bio<br />--- 16 years old, son of Mendanber and Cimorene (<i>King and Queen of Enchanted Forest</i>). He is also the narrator of this book.<br />My Feelings<br />--- This character was just amazing. I couldn't stop myself from reading just because of this character. I liked this very much. I will always remember this character.<br /><br /><b>Shiara</b><br />Bio<br />--- A fire-witch who doesn't know how to use her magic. But when she finds out: How to use her magic, I can't stop laughing. <br />My Feelings<br />--- She was also amazing but sometimes she became a bad-girl type, you know. Nevertheless I liked her. She was adorable.<br /><br /><b>A Dragon</b><br />Bio <br />--- Its gender was unknown because it was not old enough to define who is it.<br />My Feelings<br />---- It was sort of a funny character. I liked it and its comedy. It always wanted to eat every thing. I liked the scene how it entered the book.<br /><br /><i>The characters who were the focus of the previous books became the secondary characters in this book. But I did't hate hate that fact. Instead I liked how they appeared in this book.</i><br /><br /><br /><u>▌<b>OVERVIEW</b>▐</u><br />[I think this book is a sort of retelling of a tale: 'Sleeping Beauty'. I kept feeling many references from that tale while reading. I haven't read that but I have heard about it many times that I think I don't need to read it. But if someone knows about a book totally on this tale you can tell me. I may get new things from that]<br /><br />At the end of its previous book King of Enchanted Forest was captured by the Society of Wizards in some secret place in the Castle. And castle was surround by a shield, created by wizards, through which no one except for wizards can pass. Only King's Sword can break that shield which can only be handled by the right heir who was Daystar. That means only Daystar can free his father. Daystar was born at the end of its last book. So the story continues in this book.<br />This book takes place after 16 years of the previous book: Cimorene and Daystar live at the edge of Enchanted Forest. They encounter a wizard (<i>Antorell, one of the villains of the previous books and also in this book</i>). After melting him, Cimorene gives the King's Sword to Daystar and force him to go to the Enchanted Forest without telling him anything (<i>for a reason</i>). He goes and meets Shiara, who is escaping from wizards. Both are alone so they stay together and wander through the Forest. Eventually, Daystar finds his reason that Why he is in the Enchanted Forest and What he supposes to do? So, he free his father from the Wizards' trap. (<i>that's obvious, not a big revelation I think</i>)<br /><br />How simple is that: But it's not. There are adventures in this book.<br /><br /><br /><u>▌<b>LESSONS FROM THIS SERIES</b>▐ </u><br /><i>I don't have plans to follow them.</i> *wink* hehehe...<br /><br />- Always keep a handkerchief with yourself. <br />- Never take a shortcut.<br /><br /><br /><u>▌<b>THINGS I DIDN'T LIKE</b>▐</u><br />--This book was very predictable for me. I almost guessed every part of this book except for the ending. That was little unexpected but didn't look that bad. <br />--Villains were same. This whole series have the same villains: Wizards. Villains should have changed. I didn't like this fact because neither the Protagonist did any thing to kill wizards permanently nor the Antagonist did any thing to get rid of melting by Protagonist in its previous books. <br /><br />Regardless of its predictability, I liked how author wrote each scene in an excellent manner. I liked this fact in all of its books. <br /><br /><br />According to the facts I mentioned above, I would like to give:<br /><b>***4.8 Bright Stars*** </b> (<i>round off to 5 stars</i>)<br /><br /><br /><u>▌<b>BEST BOOKS OF THE SERIES GOES TO</b>▐</u><br />1. Dealing with Dragons ◄<br />2. Searching for Dragons<br />3. Calling on Dragons <br />4. Talking to Dragons ◄<br />That's my personal thinking. Different people may have different thoughts about it.<br /><br /><b>Feel free to point out my mistakes in this review or my misunderstandings about this book if there are any. I would be happy to see that.</b><br /><br /><i>Thanks for you attention...</i>^__^<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6472915746496893408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2223127890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2223127890" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2223127890?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2223127890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11833048016255866023">A very entertaining series of fantasy books for children - of all ages, as the familiar cliche says - that have many elements of classic fairy tales while the author offers us a hilarious parody of well-known myths, legends and fairy tales. Their way of writing is particularly interesting and is based mainly on the very clever confrontation between the heroes, each of which has something special. Surely in some places this humour is not particularly apt, there are some silly moments but in gener</span>
  <span id="freeText11833048016255866023" style="display:none">A very entertaining series of fantasy books for children - of all ages, as the familiar cliche says - that have many elements of classic fairy tales while the author offers us a hilarious parody of well-known myths, legends and fairy tales. Their way of writing is particularly interesting and is based mainly on the very clever confrontation between the heroes, each of which has something special. Surely in some places this humour is not particularly apt, there are some silly moments but in general the series maintains a good level, especially in the first two. So this series might not be a very great thing but are definitely four books that offer relaxation and put a smile in the face.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11833048016255866023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_878065942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/878065942" />
    <a title="Val" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10387498-val"><img alt="Val" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/878065942?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val" href="/user/show/10387498-val">Val</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer878065942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14433599274871766698">The first three books in the series are in 3rd pov, but this one is in 1st pov. This really makes the flatness of the characters stand out.<br/><br/>The main character has no thoughts. No signs of intelligence or life. The kid is a 16 year old boy scout who only shows the barest of hints of interest in the girl who is suppose to be his love interest [they end up together at the end yet it just feels forced as there isn't any flirting or romantic interest expressed in any other way etc throughout the book)</span>
  <span id="freeText14433599274871766698" style="display:none">The first three books in the series are in 3rd pov, but this one is in 1st pov. This really makes the flatness of the characters stand out.<br /><br />The main character has no thoughts. No signs of intelligence or life. The kid is a 16 year old boy scout who only shows the barest of hints of interest in the girl who is suppose to be his love interest [they end up together at the end yet it just feels forced as there isn't any flirting or romantic interest expressed in any other way etc throughout the book). He's super polite, careful, and just has no real substance (or flaws). He just simply isn't human or alive by any means.<br /><br />What do I mean when I say that? Well, there is NO emotional response or thoughts or anything when at the very end of his journey he finds out he's a prince and meets his father, a king he just saved, for the first time. What happens? NOTHING. Like...eff you so much. He's just mild and accepting and goes along with everything. No response or feelings or thoughts etc. He's not happy, overwhelmed, or any realistic intense emotion upon seeing his father, a king, for the first time in his life. I hate you author.<br /><br />The book revolves around keeping all of the information from the king's kid and sending him off into the woods. The girl that he runs into is useless and ill tempered. USELESS. She cries. Often. Over silly and stupid things. Did I say how often she cries? I need to emphasizes this here. The only thing she does through the entire series is either needs to be protected, chitchatting with the main character/stating the obvious, is merely there existing, crying, or some combination of those. <br /><br />It's rather strange how suddenly Daystar at the very end of the book shows a high level of romantic interest in her [when until that point he showed no interest in her]. Sure, she's given a few cookie cutter 'But I helped roles', however they are rather forced. I have no idea why anyone would like her, or even want her. I'm assuming it's because he grew up in the middle of the woods with only his mom around and had no friends. That is probably the only reason why he could stand her. <br /><br />That was too harsh, you say? Okay, I'll explain further why she's such a terrible character. At the beginning she's a witch who can't use her magic. Then she's able to, but with the limitation of only being able to do so after being recently polite. Instead of being happy about this, she complains and grumbles about it. At the beginning she is able to use magic 0% of the time. Her response to learning that she could use magic, but only after being polite/nice can be paraphrased by "NUOOOOO! This is the worst thing ever!" Yeah, this sort of person is pretty much universally hated.<br /><br />She is a rude idiot. For no reason. It's just her typical temperament. What a catch, Daystar!<br /><br />Last, but not least, there's the fact that there isn't any compelling reason for Daystar to go see the dragon or hang out in the dangerous forest [thus the entire book shouldn't have really happened]. He knows nothing, his mum just tells him to go and not come back until he knows why he was sent away and is given a sword. A few random strangers tell him to meet the dragon king and he does so...even though he knows the forest is incredibly dangerous and he believes that he'd be eaten as tasty dragon chow by the dragons. There is no good/understandable reason why he meets the dragon king. Just one stranger and then a lizard suggested it... Yeah, sure, that's good enough reason for me to risk my life too.<br /><br />There was a 'fake*' [read: pulled out of your bum] reason to not tell the kid about the magic sword [because then wizard/enemies will find him magically if he knew], but why the hell couldn't he be told that his father was the king, asleep, or that he needed to be saved? That's compelling reason to risk your life and meet the dragon king.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14433599274871766698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_546509878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546509878" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/372701-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329679901p2/372701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546509878?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/372701-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372701-sarah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372701-sarah?shelf=questing">questing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372701-sarah?shelf=swords-and-sorcerors">swords-and-sorcerors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372701-sarah?shelf=strong-girls">strong-girls</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546509878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13808873864762549575">So even though this is chronologically the last book in the series, PC Wrede wrote it first - the first 3 are prequels. So as I was re-reading this book I kept thinking "why, this is really quite impressive the way that PC Wrede created such an elegantly seamless backstory to this book in the form of the first three books! And she's so effortlessly woven it into the details of this story when she didn't even really know what was going to be in them!" But then I got to the end of the book and the</span>
  <span id="freeText13808873864762549575" style="display:none">So even though this is chronologically the last book in the series, PC Wrede wrote it first - the first 3 are prequels. So as I was re-reading this book I kept thinking "why, this is really quite impressive the way that PC Wrede created such an elegantly seamless backstory to this book in the form of the first three books! And she's so effortlessly woven it into the details of this story when she didn't even really know what was going to be in them!" But then I got to the end of the book and there's a whole chapter that just explains everything that happened in the first three books. I don't know - maybe she added that later when they were published? But why? - anyone who had read them would already know what happened.<br /><br />Anyway, this book is nice enough, although it does feel like the odd one out when I think of Dealing With Dragons being so in-your-face about Yes Princesses Can! but Cimorene and Morwen are relegated to very supporting characters in this one. I do wish Morwen and Telemain had just stayed friends instead of being neatly tied up at the end. They make good friends and the characterization of each of them through the series is very strong. And since we have such a good idea of who each one of them is, I can't imagine why Morwen would want to marry him. Or why he would want to marry her, honestly. Baffling.<br /><br />Mostly I wish these books were longer. That would give PC Wrede more room to work things out so that they don't feel rushed. And also I'm just sad that I'm done rereading them already.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13808873864762549575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_253721322" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253721322" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/446509-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194659951p2/446509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253721322?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/446509-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253721322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6224732751228959591">I loved the first two books in this series, but the third and this, the fourth, books, seem to be geared to a younger and younger audience. And while I love a good middle grade fantasy story, I felt this one didn't have the complexity within the plot or characters that I would have liked, and that MG readers can handle.<br/><br/>The main focus of this tale seemed to be to encourage politeness. And while I love that theme, it did feel a bit heavy handed at times.<br/><br/>For 16 years of age, I felt our protagonist </span>
  <span id="freeText6224732751228959591" style="display:none">I loved the first two books in this series, but the third and this, the fourth, books, seem to be geared to a younger and younger audience. And while I love a good middle grade fantasy story, I felt this one didn't have the complexity within the plot or characters that I would have liked, and that MG readers can handle.<br /><br />The main focus of this tale seemed to be to encourage politeness. And while I love that theme, it did feel a bit heavy handed at times.<br /><br />For 16 years of age, I felt our protagonist wasn't as mature as he should have been. He was kind and smart, and very polite, but, to me, he *sounded* younger. I did like him! But, as a protagonist who will one day be king, at 16 I would have expected a wiser protagonist.<br /><br />Also, so many times I felt that the actions of the characters were over described, or that Wrede was trying to justify an action, when either the explanation was already obvious, or when a different action really should have been taken.<br /><br />And yet, overall, it's still a nice, quick read, with main characters who try to do the right thing. And I appreciate that it's nice that the tale isn't dark, or disturbing as some MG/YA books can be. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6224732751228959591" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/662439-jo?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/662439-jo?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/662439-jo?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198089433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13601070125809880809">I would have preferred that Wrede end this series with the third book...moving on to the second generation of characters is usually not as fun. For me, the motivation of the main character just didn't seem strong enough, and while I realize that this fantasy series is meant to be lighter in tone than some of its more dramatic counterparts, the characters' emotions were a trifle too understated for my taste.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33555642-sara-saif?shelf=seriously-so-good-i-can-t-even">seriously-so-good-i-can-t-even</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674221121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9745327586280741672"><p>This series has been surprisingly wonderful! I still believe that the best book was the first one but the rest were equally magnificent. The books were light and chucklesome. Never once did I feel that things were slow or boring in all 4 books and I was glued to the spot reading. The story flowed effortlessly and managed to make perfect sense even with all the ridiculousness.</p><br/>The last book takes place roughly 16 years after the third one. This time it’s Cimorene’s son, Daystar, we follow as he at</span>
  <span id="freeText9745327586280741672" style="display:none"><p>This series has been surprisingly wonderful! I still believe that the best book was the first one but the rest were equally magnificent. The books were light and chucklesome. Never once did I feel that things were slow or boring in all 4 books and I was glued to the spot reading. The story flowed effortlessly and managed to make perfect sense even with all the ridiculousness.</p><br>The last book takes place roughly 16 years after the third one. This time it’s Cimorene’s son, Daystar, we follow as he attempts to take the sword to the castle of Enchanted Forest. The familiar characters popped up as Daystar made his journey through the forest along with his companions. That particular twist <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mendanbar being trapped in his castle and separated from Cimorene for 16 years before his grown up son could break the spell <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>was a bit unexpected for me. It added a tad seriousness to the easy-going nature of the story. <br><p>I was a little taken aback by the fact that this book was written before all others and it had to be readjusted as the last book in the series. In fact, I’m still having trouble wrapping my head around it. It also explains why, when Daystar is told his parents’ story by them, it didn’t quite match what really happened in the first three books. What he was told was actually very different.</p><br>I’m not feeling the series-hangover yet but I will, I just know it. Suffice it to say, I adored these sweet and perfect books and Cimorene’s headstrong princess will always stay close to my heart.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401586017ra/9821522.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>P.S: Actual rating is not exactly 4 stars but close.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9745327586280741672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_481332463" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481332463" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6611335-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340801408p2/6611335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481332463?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/6611335-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6611335-lara?shelf=z-2016-to-read">z-2016-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6611335-lara?shelf=z-2015-to-read">z-2015-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6611335-lara?shelf=small_town">small_town</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6611335-lara?shelf=z-2016">z-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481332463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16539242878366260640">When I first read the blurb about this book and realized it would be about Cimorene's son, I was worried. Then I started reading and it was also in the first person, which was another change. However, I quickly realized that I enjoyed this book even better than the previous three in the trilogy, though it didn't have so much of the new magical ideas and items as the other ones.<br/><br/>Daystar is now a teen and it's time for him to go help free his father, who has been magically bound his entire life. Un</span>
  <span id="freeText16539242878366260640" style="display:none">When I first read the blurb about this book and realized it would be about Cimorene's son, I was worried. Then I started reading and it was also in the first person, which was another change. However, I quickly realized that I enjoyed this book even better than the previous three in the trilogy, though it didn't have so much of the new magical ideas and items as the other ones.<br /><br />Daystar is now a teen and it's time for him to go help free his father, who has been magically bound his entire life. Unfortunately for him, while he knows a great deal about the Enchanted Forest and dragons, and even some about magic, he doesn't know that his mother is Queen or that he's a prince. He thinks they are relatively poor and his mother just knows a lot. Imagine his surprise when she shoves him off to have his adventures with nothing more than a sword she suddenly brings out of the forest.<br /><br />Daystar is very sweet and things do happen to him despite his efforts to be polite and stay out of trouble. Shiara is very talented and strong, though I found her a bit annoying for much of the book. By the end she wasn't so bad, though. Their adventures mean that they run into many of the characters we came to know and love through the trilogy; those adventures are not recapped until the very end of the book. Daystar remains ignorant as people have to figure things out on their own when on a quest in the Enchanted Forest.<br /><br />All-in-all it was a excellent wrap-up and ending to the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16539242878366260640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4966286832568382555">On the day when a wizard destroys the front door of their house, Daystar’s mother hands him a sword and tells him not to come home again until he can explain why she sent him away. Questing his way through the Enchanted Forest, Daystar befriends a lizard, a fire witch, and a young dragon, and encounters elves, dwarves, witches, wizards, and many others before his quest is complete and he learns the truth about his extraordinary sword.<br/><br/>Not my favorite of the series, but still a very good book, and</span>
  <span id="freeText4966286832568382555" style="display:none">On the day when a wizard destroys the front door of their house, Daystar’s mother hands him a sword and tells him not to come home again until he can explain why she sent him away. Questing his way through the Enchanted Forest, Daystar befriends a lizard, a fire witch, and a young dragon, and encounters elves, dwarves, witches, wizards, and many others before his quest is complete and he learns the truth about his extraordinary sword.<br /><br />Not my favorite of the series, but still a very good book, and it does an admirable job of answering the questions left unanswered at the end of the previous book. It’s a good ending to the series, but I never want the series to end — maybe that’s why I don’t love this book best of all?<br /></span>

It meant everything I didn't remember mattered little towards my enjoyment of this story. I love how this series subverts fantasy tropes. It is funny and yet no-nonsense. I really enjoyed being back in this world. This is one of my favorite children's book series.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_509541410" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/509541410" />
    <a title="Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2737449-grace"><img alt="Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471387442p2/2737449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/509541410?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/2737449-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780590484756" href="/book/show/883313.Talking_to_Dragons">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2737449-grace?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2737449-grace?shelf=fantasy-or-syfy">fantasy-or-syfy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer509541410&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer509541410" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4145649006338604768">All’s well that ends well. I found this predictable. I did enjoy how polite Daystar was to everyone, but I began to despise Shiara by the end. Traveling with someone like her in an enchanted forest? Someone who refuses to be polite even after, clearly, the bushes have made their opinion known on her prior rudeness? (I mean, if the <i>bushes</i> don’t like you…) She couldn’t even be grudgingly polite to the bushes after it was clear why they weren’t letting her out! In an enchanted forest, it doesn’t ma</span>
  <span id="freeText4145649006338604768" style="display:none">All’s well that ends well. I found this predictable. I did enjoy how polite Daystar was to everyone, but I began to despise Shiara by the end. Traveling with someone like her in an enchanted forest? Someone who refuses to be polite even after, clearly, the bushes have made their opinion known on her prior rudeness? (I mean, if the <i>bushes</i> don’t like you…) She couldn’t even be grudgingly polite to the bushes after it was clear why they weren’t letting her out! In an enchanted forest, it doesn’t matter how you feel—clearly most everything is sentient and likes human beings polite to it/them. So for goodness sake, don’t offend the bushes! They could trap you in a prickly hedge and let you starve!<br /><br />But noooo. Shiara was all, “I’m a fire-witch. People should respect me. I shouldn’t have to respect them. *insert sullen pout*” <br /><br />How was she not eaten before Daystar found her? How did Daystar <i>stand</i> her? I understand the humor of her character to some degree. She pulled no punches and could sometimes be amusing in a completely blundering, unattractively angry and disrespectful way. She moved things along when people were being overly polite. But if someone were actually <i>like</i> that in life, it would be far from amusing. I doubt someone as polite as Daystar would’ve been so patient with her if this were a real life situation.<br /><br />So, in case you couldn’t tell, Shiara grated on my nerves a lot by the end. (And how naive is Daystar to not see his mother is already setting him up with her in the future?) The rest of the cast was good. Daystar was a very polite gentleman, while still coming across a strong and lovable main character. The dragon reminded me of Killer from the previous book. However, Cimorene and Mendanbar’s reunion left much to be desired. Like, a ton to be desired. And now there’s a sixteen year (or so) gap between them, right? He didn’t have to eat where he was, and he didn’t age either, right? Goodness. But everything was shiny in the end. Everything got a nice coating of Happily Ever After. This series fits better for younger children who won’t find its unrealistic Everything Wraps Up Perfectly endings grating.<br /><br />I’m giving this two stars because, like I said before, it was very predictable. The ending also drove me nuts because that amount of explaining wasn’t needed. If you paid attention to the plot at all, the explanations were obvious. If you read the previous books, then the explanations weren’t just obvious but grating. It wrapped up happily with bad guys all eaten/melted/burned. (Of course.) I feel like this series could’ve ended at the end of the first book or second.<br /><br />But one upside is that Morwen and Telemain are finally together! About dang time too!<br /><br />Warning/heads up/what’s in this book—many wizards were melted/eaten/died in the making of this book. As well as one fire-witch. None of it was graphic, but not everyone got away unscathed (read: every wizard or bad guy, as per usual).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4145649006338604768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23786645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12530460079869603017"><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I really enjoyed this book! Part of that was the switch to first person pov, which I adore.<br/><br/>Daystar is so polite and honorable. He has some of the more dangerous adventures (a baby dragon, exploding wizard staves, transdimensional doorway traps, a firewitch with anger issues, and an entire Enchanted Forest out to help him or harm him before he can get to the castle. I'm glad he doesn't spend half his time whining and asking what is going on. He actually figures out the mystery in</span>
  <span id="freeText12530460079869603017" style="display:none"><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I really enjoyed this book! Part of that was the switch to first person pov, which I adore.<br /><br />Daystar is so polite and honorable. He has some of the more dangerous adventures (a baby dragon, exploding wizard staves, transdimensional doorway traps, a firewitch with anger issues, and an entire Enchanted Forest out to help him or harm him before he can get to the castle. I'm glad he doesn't spend half his time whining and asking what is going on. He actually figures out the mystery in the end and isn't upset that he had to be kept in the dark. Very good ending.<br /><br />I like that we get to see the familiar characters (Cimorene, the wizards, Morwen, Kazul) from the previous books through Daystar's eyes. Everyone knows who he is and what he's supposed to do, but he thinks he's just the son of a poor woman living at the edge of a magical forest. Ha!<br /><br />(Actually, his childhood isn't very believable. Why would Cimorene never have met with Morwen, Kazul, and Telemaine? Wouldn't Daystar know them? Why had he not traveled around and met everyone and know more about what's going on? Perhaps Cimorene gave him a growth potion, and she's only been hiding him for a few months. Yeah.)<br /><br /><b>Writer thoughts:</b> Why switch to a first person pov? Is it to help readers feel more grounded in this time rather than still thinking we're following the other characters 16 years ago? Or is it to keep from giving away any of the spoilers that all the other characters know but Daystar doesn't?<br /><br />Whatever it is, I like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12530460079869603017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/478604-amy?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/478604-amy?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/478604-amy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48466328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1368317863845000163">In book 4 of the Enchanted Forest Chronicles, the narrator is Daystar, Cimorene's son. He is on a sent on a quest with a magical sword. Along the way, he meets evil wizards, a fire witch named Shiara, and a young talking dragon.<br/><br/>The first time I started this book, I had not read any of the others. I read about 30 pages in a restaurant while waiting for my food because it was the only book I had with me. I didn't finish because I don't really like to read things out of order - but I was intrigued </span>
  <span id="freeText1368317863845000163" style="display:none">In book 4 of the Enchanted Forest Chronicles, the narrator is Daystar, Cimorene's son. He is on a sent on a quest with a magical sword. Along the way, he meets evil wizards, a fire witch named Shiara, and a young talking dragon.<br /><br />The first time I started this book, I had not read any of the others. I read about 30 pages in a restaurant while waiting for my food because it was the only book I had with me. I didn't finish because I don't really like to read things out of order - but I was intrigued enough to read the rest of the series once I found them at the library.<br /><br />In hindsight, I think that for the first part of the book, it works really well to not read the other books first. In order to rescue the King and break the spell of the evil wizards, Daystar must not know the significance of the sword he's carrying. If he knows the nature of the sword, the wizards can use a finding spell to find the sword. So an ignorance of the previous story makes Daystar's point of view fresher and more realistic.<br /><br />I can't recommend reading the entire book prior to reading the other three - it would spoil the others! And all four are really fun reads.<br /><br />This book was a satisfying conclusion to the series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1368317863845000163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3140627" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3140627" />
    <a title="Punk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116652-punk"><img alt="Punk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181025939p2/116652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3140627?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Punk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Punk" href="/user/show/116652-punk">Punk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116652-punk?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116652-punk?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116652-punk?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3140627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2990427803431889682">YA Fantasy. Book three in this series ends on a cliffhanger and book four picks up sixteen years later. That was unexpected. We've also got a new narrator for this one: Daystar, a very polite, logical young man, whose mother slaps a sword in his hand and sends him off into the Enchanted Forest one day without really telling him why. His mother is, of course, Queen Cimorene, and his dad's off in a magical coma, but Daystar doesn't know any of that. He's just trying to make sense of this sudden ne</span>
  <span id="freeText2990427803431889682" style="display:none">YA Fantasy. Book three in this series ends on a cliffhanger and book four picks up sixteen years later. That was unexpected. We've also got a new narrator for this one: Daystar, a very polite, logical young man, whose mother slaps a sword in his hand and sends him off into the Enchanted Forest one day without really telling him why. His mother is, of course, Queen Cimorene, and his dad's off in a magical coma, but Daystar doesn't know any of that. He's just trying to make sense of this sudden need for him to go on some unexplained quest. Along the way he meets a young dragon and a fire-witch with a temper and they all work together to get Daystar where he needs to be. <br /><br />This book's as good as the first in the series, and for the same reasons. Daystar's plucky like his mom, good with magic like his dad, and just a smart, funny narrator. He's also a first person narrator, which kept throwing me for some odd reason. Probably because it read more like a very removed third person, so the pronouns kept surprising me. <br /><br />Four stars. A nice end to this series and a lot of fun all on its own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2990427803431889682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2783146120" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2783146120" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590863781p2/3498889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2783146120?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2783146120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14909517982230229224">I've done reading the whole series, so will copy these comments to 3rd and 4th book, too.<br/><br/>Love the humor. Love the breezy adventure and endearing characters. Each book focuses on different folks, but the sequence events counts, and I do not recommend trying to read them as stand-alones. The ending of #2 is a bit worrisome, and the ending of #3 is a cliff-hanger, and #4 does have some intensity not necessarily suitable for the youngest readers. On the whole, they're clean and fun, I'd say fine for</span>
  <span id="freeText14909517982230229224" style="display:none">I've done reading the whole series, so will copy these comments to 3rd and 4th book, too.<br /><br />Love the humor. Love the breezy adventure and endearing characters. Each book focuses on different folks, but the sequence events counts, and I do not recommend trying to read them as stand-alones. The ending of #2 is a bit worrisome, and the ending of #3 is a cliff-hanger, and #4 does have some intensity not necessarily suitable for the youngest readers. On the whole, they're clean and fun, I'd say fine for ages 9 up but if your younger child wants to read them you should also. <br /><br />Um, they're also not really memorable - they're probably best suited for people who like to reread books because there's a lot going on, but nothing heavy enough to make an impact on the reader's worldview. I know it's partly my fault because I read them so fast - but then, they were fast reads, and I couldn't help it.<br /><br />*at least, I didn't find them to be memorable. I'm sure kids would, and probably some adults.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14909517982230229224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23420000" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23420000" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/417378-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381880980p2/417378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23420000?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/417378-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/417378-diana?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/417378-diana?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/417378-diana?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/417378-diana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/417378-diana?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/417378-diana?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23420000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4221314204649955057">It's been sixteen years since the events in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/169879.Calling_on_Dragons__The_Enchanted_Forest_Chronicles__Book_3_' title='Calling on Dragons (The Enchanted Forest Chronicles, Book 3) by Patricia C. Wrede' rel='nofollow noopener'>Calling On Dragons</a> and Daystar has been raised by his mother Cimorene, not knowing his true heritage. When the wizards finally track them down, Cimorene sends Daystar with the magical sword into the Enchanted Forest on a mysterious quest.<br/><br/>This was a little different, with Daystar being the first-person narrator. He's a very interesting narrator, and brings a fresh perspective on things. I was a little annoyed that no one would tell him anything and ever</span>
  <span id="freeText4221314204649955057" style="display:none">It's been sixteen years since the events in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/169879.Calling_on_Dragons__The_Enchanted_Forest_Chronicles__Book_3_" title="Calling on Dragons (The Enchanted Forest Chronicles, Book 3) by Patricia C. Wrede" rel="nofollow noopener">Calling On Dragons</a> and Daystar has been raised by his mother Cimorene, not knowing his true heritage. When the wizards finally track them down, Cimorene sends Daystar with the magical sword into the Enchanted Forest on a mysterious quest.<br /><br />This was a little different, with Daystar being the first-person narrator. He's a very interesting narrator, and brings a fresh perspective on things. I was a little annoyed that no one would tell him anything and everyone insisted on being vague and mysterious--there didn't seem to be much point to it except to make a better story. I also though that the long-awaited family reunion was a bit lackluster--especially after seventeen years!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4221314204649955057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Lr/im0aW8wAJ4UA3r/ypF1upDEwziaNmUNjugvpZA/zz8gAxxtlCxFfuuvk3dNYVmYNGB2EWZBkf/BuS+8TVKw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bFmKSx8SKZPx/zbnP1RC9OADu+LYB44wxjm91clTpTaxFGjhn12YV6/wzCmn3D32IinxqYqYSU+JHUjFyM5z4Q==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/36122.Patricia_C_Wrede">About Patricia C. Wrede</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/36122.Patricia_C_Wrede"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1572816128p3/36122.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/36122.Patricia_C_Wrede">Patricia C. Wrede
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5698294538762522791">Patricia Collins Wrede was born in Chicago, Illinois and is the eldest of five children. She started writing in seventh grade. She attended Carleton College in Minnesota, where she majored in Biology and managed to avoid taking any English courses at all. She began work on her first novel, Shadow Magic, just after graduating from college in 1974. She finished it five years later and started her se</span>
  <span id="freeText5698294538762522791" style="display:none">Patricia Collins Wrede was born in Chicago, Illinois and is the eldest of five children. She started writing in seventh grade. She attended Carleton College in Minnesota, where she majored in Biology and managed to avoid taking any English courses at all. She began work on her first novel, Shadow Magic, just after graduating from college in 1974. She finished it five years later and started her second book at once, having become permanently hooked on writing by this time.<br /><br />Patricia received her M.B.A. from the University of Minnesota in 1977.<br />She worked for several years as a financial analyst and accountant, first with the Minnesota Hospital Association, then with B. Dalton Booksellers, and finally at the Dayton Hudson Corporation headquarters.<br /><br />Patricia finished her first novel in late 1978. In January, 1980, Pamela Dean, Emma Bull, Will Shetterly, Steven Brust, Nate Bucklin, and Patricia Wrede -- all, at that point, hopeful but unpublished -- formed the writer's group that later became known as "The Scribblies." Several years later, they were joined by Kara Dalkey. In April of 1980, Patricia's first novel sold to Ace Books. It came out at last in 1982, which is the year she met Lillian Stewart Carl (who introduced her to Lois McMaster Bujold by mail).<br /><br />In 1985, shortly before the publication of her fifth book, she left the world of the gainfully employed to try winging it on her own.<br /><br />Her interests include sewing, embroidery, desultory attempts at gardening, chocolate, not mowing the lawn, High Tea, and, of course, reading.<br />She is a vegetarian, and currently lives in Minneapolis, Minnesota with her cat Karma. She has no children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5698294538762522791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
